# JANG Studio Production Audit Checklist

**Populated by Ralph Loop iteration 1 — 2026-04-19.**
Source-of-truth for subsequent Ralph iterations: each iteration reads this file, picks the next `[ ]` item, verifies or fixes, marks `[x]` with commit SHA + note.

The goal: every item reaches `[x]` with production-ready behavior. "Production" means it matches the documented rules in `~/.claude/projects/-Users-eric-jang/memory/` AND the actual behavior is verified, not assumed.

**How each item is closed:**
- Read the memory file(s) referenced
- Verify the app/CLI/bundle does what the rule requires
- If behavior drifts: fix it, commit, add the SHA next to the item
- If behavior matches: add a one-line verification note next to the item
- Mark `[x]` only when verified with evidence

---

## A. Conversion output integrity (jang-tools side)

- [ ] **A01** — `jang_config.json` writes `format=="jang"`, `format_version` `"2.x"+`, non-empty `capabilities`, correct `quantization.bit_widths_used`. (Referenced by `PostConvertVerifier` rows #1-#4.)
- [ ] **A02** — `capabilities` stamp includes `arch`, `reasoning`, `tool`, `cache`, `modality`. Cross-check every arch in `jang_tools/capabilities.py` FAMILY_MAP maps correctly (see commit `43af293` for llama+idefics3 gap).
- [ ] **A03** — `config.json` output preserves original `_name_or_path` so HF model cards auto-generate with correct `base_model`.
- [ ] **A04** — Qwen3.5 eos auto-fix: 248044 → 248046 applied to top-level, `text_config`, AND `tokenizer_config.json`. Source of rule: `feedback_chat_template_rules.md`.
- [ ] **A05** — MiniMax eos_token_id 200020 ([e~[) preserved. Source: `feedback_chat_template_rules.md`.
- [ ] **A06** — Nemotron eos_token_id 2 preserved + standard ChatML intact.
- [ ] **A07** — `generation_config.json` copied when present in source. Cross-check convert.py extra_configs list.
- [ ] **A08** — All tokenizer files copied: `tokenizer.json` OR `tokenizer.model` + `tokenizer_config.json` + `special_tokens_map.json` + `merges.txt` + `vocab.json` + `added_tokens.json` when present.
- [ ] **A09** — Chat template preserved in AT LEAST ONE of three forms: inline in `tokenizer_config.json`, `chat_template.jinja`, or `chat_template.json`. `PostConvertVerifier` accepts any of three (confirmed via A16 audit row).
- [ ] **A10** — Chat template `enable_thinking` toggle preserved (MiniMax default is always-on — must be made toggleable). Source: `feedback_chat_template_rules.md`.
- [ ] **A11** — `tokenizer_class` remapped from `TokenizersBackend` → concrete class (e.g. `GPT2Tokenizer`) for Osaurus compatibility.
- [ ] **A12** — `modeling_*.py` + `configuration_*.py` + custom parser `.py` files copied for trust_remote_code models (MiniMax, Nemotron).
- [ ] **A13** — Shard naming: `model-NNNNN-of-MMMMM.safetensors`. Index file `model.safetensors.index.json` references exactly those files. No leftover `model-*-of-NNNNN.safetensors` placeholder files.

## B. VL and video model handling (feedback_always_vl.md + feedback_jang_studio_audit_coverage.md)

- [ ] **B01** — `preprocessor_config.json` ALWAYS copied from source when present. Verified in Ralph audit A11 on SmolVLM (pixel_values [1,17,3,512,512]).
- [ ] **B02** — `video_preprocessor_config.json` ALWAYS copied from source when present (Qwen3.5 models ship this — cannot be silently dropped).
- [ ] **B03** — VL image path: `AutoProcessor.from_pretrained(model_dir, trust_remote_code=True)(images=image, text="...", return_tensors="pt")` returns non-empty `pixel_values`. Ralph A11.
- [ ] **B04** — Video path: `AutoProcessor` accepts `videos=frames` kwarg and returns `pixel_values_videos`. Ralph A12 (currently n/a — no video model in tier 1).
- [ ] **B05** — `inspect-source --json` emits `is_vl` AND `is_video_vl` as distinct booleans (not a single `is_vl` flag). Source: `feedback_jang_studio_audit_coverage.md`.
- [ ] **B06** — Swift `ArchitectureSummary` has both `isVL` and `isVideoVL`. PostConvertVerifier row #8b gated on `isVideoVL`.
- [ ] **B07** — Ralph fixtures `test_image.png` (64×64 RGB) and `test_video_frames.npy` (16×32×32×3) exist + gitignored exceptions in place. Verified commit `baed27a`.

## C. Model-specific architecture rules

- [ ] **C01** — 512+ expert models force `bfloat16` (source: `project_bfloat16_fix.md`). `KNOWN_512_EXPERT_TYPES` includes minimax_m2, glm_moe_dsa. Now served via `jang-tools capabilities --json`.
- [ ] **C02** — MLP asymmetry: 512+ expert models use gate_proj=4-bit floor, down_proj=3-bit floor (source: `project_mlp_asymmetry.md`). Verify `allocate.py` applies this when expert count ≥ 512.
- [ ] **C03** — `project_mistral4_architecture.md` 6 fixes active for MLA+MoE: FP8 bf16 scale, rope_interleave, norm_topk_prob, llama4_beta, PLAIN attention scale (no mscale²), gate dequant.
- [ ] **C04** — Qwen3.6 hybrid SSM (GatedDeltaNet + full-attn + 256 routed + 1 shared + MTP + MRoPE). Verify conversion produces all tensor classes. Source: `project_qwen36.md`.
- [ ] **C05** — Cascade-2 Nemotron-H 128-expert Mamba-hybrid converts correctly. Source: `project_cascade2.md`.
- [ ] **C06** — MiniMax-M2.7 FP8 source loads via `load_fp8_tensor` with correct scale application. Source: `project_minimax_m27.md`.
- [ ] **C07** — JANGTQ Qwen3.6 + MiniMax conversion scripts exist and work (`convert_qwen35_jangtq.py` + `convert_minimax_jangtq.py`). GLM JANGTQ is deferred to v1.1.

## D. Progress bar / phase tracking (JSONL protocol v1)

- [ ] **D01** — Every long-running CLI emits phase+tick events: `convert`, `convert_qwen35_jangtq`, `convert_minimax_jangtq`. Verified in Phase 1 commits.
- [ ] **D02** — Swift `PythonRunner` parses JSONL stderr reliably; malformed lines don't kill the run (JSONLProgressParser `.parseError` event).
- [ ] **D03** — Step 4 macro progress bar shows `[N/5] name` for all 5 phases: detect, calibrate, allocate, quantize, write.
- [ ] **D04** — Step 4 fine progress bar updates per tensor during quantize phase. Tick throttle respects user setting (default 100ms, range 50-500ms from Settings → Advanced).
- [ ] **D05** — ETA display — not yet implemented (spec Part 12). Gap — add ETA calculation based on tick throughput.
- [ ] **D06** — Memory pressure monitor — not yet implemented (spec Part 12). Gap — add live `host_statistics64` polling.
- [ ] **D07** — Cancel button fires SIGTERM → 3s → SIGKILL per `PythonRunner.cancel`. Verified in XCTest `test_cancelSIGTERMLandsWithinThreeSeconds`.
- [ ] **D08** — Pause/Resume (SIGSTOP/SIGCONT) — not yet implemented. Gap — spec Part 12 Step 4 enhancement.

## G. Directory permissions / error handling

- [ ] **G01** — Source dir read-only → convert succeeds (write only to output dir).
- [ ] **G02** — Output dir not writable → preflight catches it before convert starts (row #3 outputUsable).
- [ ] **G03** — Output dir == source dir → preflight fail (prevents overwriting source).
- [ ] **G04** — Output dir inside `.app` → preflight fail.
- [ ] **G05** — Disk full mid-convert → graceful error (PythonException category in spec §4.3); diagnostics bundle captures the error.
- [ ] **G06** — Cancel mid-convert → partial output left on disk by default; can be deleted via "Delete partial" banner.

Beginner summary + warnings + InfoHint tooltips shown in new "Recommended for this model" section. Step 1 now renders the full recommendation block below the Detected card.

## M. Deep-trace discoveries (spawned during Ralph iterations)

Each item here was surfaced by a concrete trace, not speculation. Each traces back to the `INVESTIGATION_LOG.md` entry that found it.

- [x] **M01** — Picking a folder with `config.json` but zero `.safetensors` silently passed Step 1 (Continue button active, user progressed to Architecture with empty detected).
      **Trace:** user picks `/tmp/empty-cfg` → `inspect-source` succeeds with `shard_count=0` → `SourceDetector` builds `ArchitectureSummary(totalBytes=0, shardCount=0)` → `isStep1Complete` returned `true` because it only checked `detected != nil`.
      **Fix:** gate `isStep1Complete` on `shardCount > 0`; show red "No .safetensors found" hint in Detected card.
      **Evidence:** `ConversionPlan.swift:57-64`, `SourceStep.swift:80-88`. 65 XCTest still pass.
      **Commit:** (this iteration)
- [ ] **M02** — Error path: user picks a folder that LOOKS model-shaped but is actually a different HF repo clone (e.g., a dataset with config.json). Verify inspect-source + recommend don't hard-crash.
- [ ] **M03** — Drag-and-drop folder onto Step 1 — spec (design addendum Part 5) promises this; implementation uses only NSOpenPanel. Missing feature.
- [ ] **M04** — Recents list for source dirs — missing. If user cancels mid-convert and wants to retry, they re-pick from scratch.
- [x] **M05** — PreflightRunner size estimate when `detected.totalBytes == 0` — current fallback returns pass with free-GB hint, but does the UI make clear that "no estimate" ≠ "safe"?
      **Close (iter 101):** pre-M05 the uncheckable branch returned `.pass` with `"X GB free"` — visually identical to a real positive check. User couldn't tell whether the system had actually verified sufficient space or simply couldn't compute an estimate yet (pre-inspection, unknown profile). Changed to `.warn` with `"X GB free (no estimate yet — pick source + profile for a real check)"`. Warn doesn't block preflight like fail would, but makes the uncheckable state UI-visible so the user knows to return to the check after picking source + profile.
      **Tests (+2) in PreflightRunnerTests.swift:**
      - `test_diskSpace_pre_inspection_warns_about_uncheckable_state` — plan with source + output + profile but no detected size → asserts `.warn` + `"no estimate"` in hint.
      - `test_diskSpace_post_inspection_with_room_still_passes` — regression guard: with a real estimate + sufficient free space, still `.pass`.
      **Evidence:** `JANGStudio/JANGStudio/Verify/PreflightRunner.swift:170-188`. 26 PreflightRunnerTests pass (was 24, +2).
- [ ] **M06** — Conflict detection: if `config.json.model_type = minimax_m2` but `tokenizer_config.json.tokenizer_class = Qwen2Tokenizer`, does the app detect the conflict? Probably silent today.
- [ ] **M07** — Nested model_type: all known patterns are `text_config.model_type`. Verify no real HF multimodal uses `llm_config.model_type` or similar non-standard keys. Current code only falls back to `text_config`.
- [ ] **M08** — Model directory that's a symlink or on a read-only volume — does the rsync / copy during convert survive? What error does the user see?
- [ ] **M09** — User picks the SAME folder as their output → Preflight catches this (`outputUsable` row). But what if user picks output as a subfolder of source? Still bad, not caught today.
- [ ] **M10** — Settings pane → change `pythonOverridePath` → pick a folder → verify `BundleResolver.pythonExecutable` reads the new value. Does it require an app restart?
- [ ] **M11** — User changes output naming template mid-flow (Step 3 already open, switches profile, does output dir name update?). Test that the auto-computed output path re-renders on profile change.
- [x] **M12** — Step 4 Cancel → Retry: previously Cancel flipped `plan.run` to `.succeeded` (major bug — user saw "Continue → Verify" after cancelling). Retry did reconstruct PythonRunner cleanly, but the UI state was lying about success.
      **Fix:** track `cancelRequested` @State in RunStep; after the for-await loop exits without throw, branch on it — set `.cancelled` vs `.succeeded`. Old SIGKILL-after-3s Task captures `proc` strongly so even if user hits Retry immediately, the zombie timer targets the correct process (no PID-reuse risk).
      **Evidence:** `RunStep.swift:75-95` (start method), `RunStep.swift:42-56` (cancelled UI branch). 65 XCTest still pass.
      **Commit:** (this iteration)
- [x] **M13** — Stale log visibility when navigating back to Run step: SwiftUI `@State` preserves the `logs` array across navigation; new start() does `logs.removeAll()` at top. User navigating back mid-run sees current live log. User navigating back to a finished run (succeeded/failed/cancelled) sees the historical log — correct behavior.
      **Evidence:** `RunStep.swift:78` (`logs.removeAll()` at start), `RunStep.swift:72` (onAppear guard via `guard coord.plan.run != .running else { return }`).
- [x] **M14** — Double-click Start Conversion: `start()` first-line guard `guard coord.plan.run != .running else { return }` rejects re-entry. First call sets `.running` before any async work; second-click call returns immediately. Cancel button now additionally `.disabled(cancelRequested)` to prevent double-cancel.
      **Evidence:** `RunStep.swift:20` cancel disabled-state; `RunStep.swift:75` start re-entry guard.
- [x] **M15** — Swift publish dialog stored the HF token in `@State private var token: String` — after a successful upload it stayed in memory until the sheet was dismissed. A passerby at the user's Mac could copy the value out of the SecureField buffer (or it could surface in a memory snapshot during a crash dump sent for a bug report). No leak path today, but leaving a secret in memory longer than needed is defense-in-depth hygiene.
      **Fix (iter 17):** `runPublish()` wipes `token = ""` on success after `publishResult = r`. On FAILURE we intentionally keep the token so the user can retry without retyping — a ~30-second exposure window while troubleshooting is better UX than forcing re-entry on every failed attempt.
      **Evidence:** `PublishToHuggingFaceSheet.swift:175-179`.
      **Commit:** (this iteration)
- [x] **M16 + M22e** — DiagnosticsBundle zipped raw log + event strings with no scrubbing. If a convert or publish failed with an HF-token-leaking exception (HfHubHTTPError embedding Authorization header), the token would land in run.log/events.jsonl inside a bug-report zip sent to GitHub Issues → credentials in the public tracker. Iter 6 scrubbed tokens at the publish-error call site, but any OTHER entry point (debug-mode HTTPX logs, future error paths, user pasting a token into a prompt field) still leaked.
      **Fix (iter 14):** `DiagnosticsBundle.scrubSensitive(_:)` applies 4 regex patterns before writing: `hf_…`, `huggingface_…`, `Authorization: Bearer …`, generic `Bearer …` (all ≥20-char suffix to avoid matching incidental variable names like `hf_short`). Matches replaced with `<redacted>`. Called on every log line AND every event line before `String.write(to:)`. End-to-end test unzips a bundle and asserts the raw secret does not appear in ANY file.
      **Evidence:** `DiagnosticsBundle.swift:7-35` (patterns + scrubber), 7 new tests including end-to-end unzip-and-grep.
      **Commit:** (this iteration)
- [ ] **M17** — TestInferenceSheet temperature slider: min=0.0, max=2.0 — what happens at exactly 0.0? (greedy decode) What about float precision edge cases?
- [ ] **M18** — Cancel during HF model download on macstudio: Ralph runner calls `snapshot_download(repo_id)` — cancellation here requires SIGTERM on the whole python3 subprocess. Does it clean up partial safetensors? HF's lock files?
- [x] **M19** — TestInferenceSheet Cancel during generate: confirmed `InferenceRunner.generate()` blocked on `proc.waitUntilExit()` while holding the actor — same deadlock we fixed in PythonRunner at commit `6270214`. Fixed iter 3: replaced `waitUntilExit()` with `withCheckedContinuation + terminationHandler`, added `cancelled` actor state + `InferenceError.cancelledCode=-2` sentinel, `TestInferenceViewModel` now filters cancelled errors so UI doesn't show a red banner on deliberate cancel.
- [ ] **M20** — StepCancel → Convert another: `reset()` in VerifyStep creates a new `ConversionPlan()` but the old PythonRunner in Step 4 may still have a SIGKILL-after-3s Task pending. Does orphaned task leak memory or fire an unnecessary kill?
- [ ] **M21** — App quit while convert is running: macOS sends TerminationRequest to the app, which dies — does the bundled Python subprocess get SIGTERM via process group, or does it orphan and keep running? (Likely orphans — bundled python under app has no formal tie to the parent once Process.run() returns.)
- [x] **M22** — Copy Diagnostics bundle race. Reviewed in iter 14: `logs` and `events` are SwiftUI `@State` arrays — mutations are MainActor-serialized. When the user clicks Copy Diagnostics, they pass snapshots (value-semantics copy) into `DiagnosticsBundle.write`, so no on-disk race. BUT three subtler bugs found + fixed in the same trace:
      - **M22d**: Timestamp was second-resolution; two clicks in the same second landed in the same workDir with stale files. Fixed with `[.withInternetDateTime, .withFractionalSeconds]` ISO formatting so each click gets a unique zip.
      - **M22e**: Tokens in logs weren't scrubbed. See M16 above.
      - **M62-anonymize**: `plan.sourceURL` / `plan.outputURL` leaked filesystem layout in bug reports. Wired to `settings.anonymizePathsInDiagnostics` — when on, paths become basenames. Call site in `RunStep.swift:64-71` passes the setting through.
      **Note:** The ORIGINAL M22 question (race on @State array) is a non-issue given SwiftUI's MainActor isolation, but the broader "is Copy Diagnostics safe mid-convert" audit surfaced 3 real bugs.
      **Evidence:** `DiagnosticsBundle.swift:45-102` (millisecond stamp, anonymize dispatch, scrubbed writes), `RunStep.swift:64-71` (setting plumbed through), 10 new Swift tests.
      **Commit:** (this iteration)
- [x] **M216 (Swift `JANGTokenizer.decode` parity with Python `tokenizer.decode`)** — Iter-145 angle-J round-2 (iter-144 was G; J was the stalest unfinished round-1 angle). Complements M208's encode-parity invariant: M208 pinned "same string → same IDs" (encode direction); M216 pins "same IDs → same string" (decode direction). Without decode parity, Swift's test-inference UI could render model output differently than Python's inference CLI even when the model emits identical IDs — a user-visible trust breaker.
      **Live evidence captured iter-145:**
      ```
      python3 -c "from transformers import AutoTokenizer; tok = ...
        for s in STRINGS:
            ids = tok.encode(s, add_special_tokens=False)
            decoded = tok.decode(ids, skip_special_tokens=True)
            print(s, ids, decoded, s == decoded)"
      ```
      Output against Qwen3.6-35B-A3B-JANG_2L:
      - `'Hello, world!'` → `[9419, 11, 1814, 0]` → `'Hello, world!'` (roundtrip=True)
      - `'The quick brown fox jumps over the lazy dog.'` → 10-token list → original (roundtrip=True)
      - `'What is 2 + 2?'` → `[3710, 369, 220, 17, 478, 220, 17, 30]` → original (roundtrip=True)
      All 3 Python references round-trip cleanly. Any Swift decode output that DIFFERS from these is a parity bug.
      **Fix (iter 145):** added two regression tests to `jang-runtime/Tests/JANGTests/JANGTokenizerPythonParityTests.swift`:
      - `test_swift_decode_matches_python_on_same_ids` — for each (string, ids) pair from the Python reference, assert `Swift.decode(ids) == Python.decode(ids)`. Cross-language decode invariant.
      - `test_swift_encode_decode_roundtrips` — assert `Swift.decode(Swift.encode(s)) == s`. Same-language round-trip invariant. Complementary safety net: a Swift encoder AND decoder that drift in mutually-canceling ways would pass the cross-language test if both matched the Python IDs but produced different strings — but would fail round-trip. Both tests together close that gap.
      **Test result: 2/2 M216 tests pass.** Swift `JANGTokenizer.decode` produces byte-identical output to Python on all 3 reference pairs. The BPE byte-encoder/decoder map is inverse-consistent.
      **Design parity with M208:**
      - Same fixture path (`/Users/eric/models/Qwen3.6-35B-A3B-JANG_2L`).
      - Same XCTSkip-when-fixture-missing pattern for CI friendliness.
      - Same hardcoded Python-reference approach (no cross-call at test time).
      - Same test-strings choice — pins that encode AND decode match Python on identical inputs.
      **Evidence:** `jang-runtime/Tests/JANGTests/JANGTokenizerPythonParityTests.swift:120-175` (new tests). 66/66 jang-runtime tests pass (was 64, +2). `swift test --filter JANGTokenizerPythonParityTests` captures concrete output: "Executed 4 tests, with 0 failures in 3.999 seconds".
      **Meta-lesson — round-2 of a parity angle expands COVERAGE, not technique.** M208 established the pattern (capture Python reference, hardcode as XCTAssertEqual targets, XCTSkip on missing fixture). M216 applies the SAME technique to the inverse operation. Same code shape, same test-design choices, different covered behavior. **Rule: when a parity-testing infrastructure is working for one direction, the round-2 extension should reuse the same pattern for the complementary direction rather than inventing a new technique. Consistency of test shape across parity directions makes the pair cheaper to maintain + clearer for future contributors.** Parallels iter-133 M196's "widen tuple rather than invent convention" — reuse pattern, extend scope.
      **Meta-lesson — encode parity and decode parity are independent invariants, not redundant.** If Swift encoder AND decoder both had mutually-canceling bugs (unlikely but possible), `decode(encode(s)) == s` could pass while both directions diverged from Python. Only the CROSS-LANGUAGE check catches that. Conversely, cross-language parity on a single direction (encode or decode) doesn't prove round-trip — the Swift encoder could agree with Python while Swift decoder silently mangles. Both checks needed. **Rule: for bijective parity across implementations (encoder/decoder, compressor/decompressor, serializer/deserializer), write TWO invariant families: cross-language parity in each direction + same-language round-trip. All three together are redundant in the happy case but catch distinct failure modes.**
      **Meta-lesson — decode parity is a UX invariant, not just a correctness one.** A Swift UI showing model output via `decode(...)` that differs from the Python test-inference CLI is confusing and erodes trust even if both outputs are "valid". Users comparing two runtimes should see identical strings. **Rule: when a runtime has multiple presentation surfaces (Swift UI, Python CLI, remote inference API), decode/format parity is load-bearing for trust. Users who notice differences will assume the app is buggy, whether it technically is or not.** Applies beyond tokenization — any formatter that touches user-visible output.
      **Commit:** (this iteration)
- [x] **M214 (HF repo-name prefill sanitizer — unicode/space auto-slug with user-visible hint)** — Iter-144 angle-G round-2 (iter-143 was H). Adversarial-user scenario: strangers with non-ASCII filesystem names (`~/café-model/`, `~/📁models/`, `~/my model (final)/`) who click Publish and get a cryptic `HFRepoValidator` error on the auto-prefilled repo name.
      **Live trace (iter 144):**
      - Built a real unicode-path fixture: `mkdir -p "/tmp/🍕-model-test"`, copied config.json from a real Qwen3.6 bundle.
      - Ran `python3 -m jang_tools inspect-source --json "/tmp/🍕-model-test"` → **success** (model_type=qwen3_5_moe correctly detected). Python subprocess argv handles unicode via UTF-8 encoding.
      - Ran `python3 -m jang_tools recommend --model "/tmp/🍕-model-test" --json` → success. JSON output ASCII-escapes emoji (`\ud83c\udf55`) but round-trips correctly.
      - Ran `python3 -m jang_tools convert "/tmp/🍕-model-test" -o "/tmp/🍕-output" -p JANG_4K` → ran through architecture detection, capabilities, output-path resolution; failed at `min(bit_widths)` empty-iterable (fixture had no safetensors, not a unicode bug).
      - Tested APFS normalization: `os.path.isdir(nfc) and os.path.isdir(nfd)` both True. APFS is normalization-insensitive, Python handles unicode paths fine.
      - **Real finding:** `PublishToHuggingFaceSheet.swift:47` pre-fills the repo-name TextField with `modelPath.lastPathComponent` AS-IS. A user whose source is `~/café-model/` gets prefill `café-model` — which `HFRepoValidator`'s ASCII-only regex `^[A-Za-z0-9][A-Za-z0-9_.-]{0,95}$` rejects with cryptic `"Invalid name segment 'café-model': start with a letter/digit, then letters/digits/._- up to 96 chars."`. The stranger doesn't know WHICH character is the problem, WHAT HF expects, or HOW to fix it.
      **Fix (iter 144):** added `HFRepoValidator.sanitizeForRepoName(_:)` and wired it into the PublishToHuggingFaceSheet init prefill:
      - **Sanitization algorithm (PublishService.swift:79-136):**
        1. NFD decomposition + ASCII-only filter (strips combining marks — `é` → `e`).
        2. Replace disallowed chars (`[^A-Za-z0-9._-]`) with `-`.
        3. Collapse `--` / `..` runs to single char (validator rejects consecutive).
        4. Trim leading/trailing `-` `.` (validator rejects trailing).
        5. If first char isn't `[A-Za-z0-9]`, prefix with `m-`.
        6. Empty result → fallback `"model"`.
      - **Return shape:** `Sanitized` struct with `sanitized: String` + `wasChanged: Bool`. Callers read `wasChanged` to decide whether to show a hint banner.
      - **Prefill wiring (PublishToHuggingFaceSheet.swift:44-65):** init runs the basename through `sanitizeForRepoName`; stores `wasChanged` in new `@State private var sanitizedHint: String?` so the Repository section can render an explanatory banner when sanitization happened.
      - **Banner content:** `"Repo name auto-sanitized from 'café-model' → 'cafe-model' (HuggingFace requires ASCII letters/digits/.-_). Edit if you'd prefer a different name."` — names the transformation, explains WHY (HF constraint), tells user they can edit. Stranger-friendly.
      **Tests (+8) in `JANGStudio/Tests/JANGStudioTests/AdoptionServicesTests.swift`:**
      - `test_sanitize_ascii_preserves_unchanged` — no false-positive sanitization banner on already-valid basenames.
      - `test_sanitize_accents_stripped` — `café-model` → `cafe-model` + passes validator downstream.
      - `test_sanitize_emoji_replaced` — `🍕-pizza` → `pizza` (emoji replaced, leading `-` trimmed).
      - `test_sanitize_spaces_to_dashes` — `my model (final)` → validator-passing slug.
      - `test_sanitize_collapses_double_dashes` — `a  b` (two spaces) doesn't produce `--`.
      - `test_sanitize_leading_non_alphanum_prefixed` — `_underscore-start` gets `m-` prefix so segment regex passes.
      - `test_sanitize_all_invalid_returns_fallback` — `🍕🍕🍕` → `"model"` fallback.
      - `test_sanitize_empty_input_returns_fallback` — empty string → `"model"` fallback.
      Each test also asserts `HFRepoValidator.validationError("org/" + sanitized)` returns nil — proves the sanitizer output passes the REAL validator, not just my synthetic shape check.
      **Evidence:** `JANGStudio/JANGStudio/Runner/PublishService.swift:79-136` (sanitizer). `JANGStudio/JANGStudio/Wizard/PublishToHuggingFaceSheet.swift:44-65` (prefill wiring), `:142-153` (banner). `xcodebuild build-for-testing` clean. 31/31 AdoptionServicesTests pass (was 23, +8).
      **Meta-lesson — adversarial scenarios fall out of real-world locale diversity.** Every user outside US-ASCII English will have filesystem names the app never tested: French `é`, German `ü`, Japanese `日本`, Chinese `模型`, Korean `모델`, emoji folder-art. US-centric dev setups never surface these. **Rule: when auditing any code path that consumes filesystem names (paths, basenames, file lookups), test with a non-ASCII fixture BEFORE shipping. The test doesn't need elaborate — a single `🍕-model` in a temp dir catches most of the class.** Builds directly on iter-143's "test byte-AND-semantic" rule: preservation claims must survive non-ASCII inputs.
      **Meta-lesson — slugify at the PREFILL point, not the validation point.** Alternate fix: keep the prefill as-is but improve the error message to say "Try replacing `café` with `cafe`". That's worse UX: user has to edit the field, the auto-prefill is a lie, and error messages are harder to write than sanitizers. Fix the prefill so it STARTS valid; add a banner explaining what we did if non-trivial. **Rule: for validation-gated input fields, sanitize at prefill time when possible. Errors should be for what the user TYPED, not for what the app prefilled.** Parallels iter-131 M194's "response body redaction" — fix at the producer, not the consumer.
      **Meta-lesson — surface sanitization, don't hide it.** A silent sanitization (prefill comes out `cafe-model` with no hint) feels magical / confusing. The user might not remember their folder was `café-model` specifically and wonder why `cafe-model` feels wrong. The banner tells them EXACTLY what happened + why + that they can edit. **Rule: when the app transforms user input automatically, show the transform inline. Invisible "helpful" transforms are a trust-breaker when discovered later.** Third corollary to the iter-123 `feedback_dont_lie_to_user.md` memory rule.
      **Meta-lesson — test the composed invariant, not just the unit.** Each M214 test asserts both that the sanitizer produced expected output AND that the output passes `HFRepoValidator.validationError`. A sanitizer that produces output matching some shape but still failing the downstream validator would silently bypass the unit-pin but break in production. **Rule: tests that bridge producer → consumer should assert the CONSUMER accepts the PRODUCER's output, not just that the producer matches a static expectation.** Parallels iter-134 M197's consumer-reference pin.
      **Commit:** (this iteration)
- [x] **M212 (eos-fix extended to `generation_config.json` — closes a silent inference-breaker)** — Iter-143 angle-H round-2. Target: byte-verify `generation_config.json` preservation against memory rule A07 + interaction with A04 (Qwen3.5 eos 248044→248046 auto-fix). Found a real inference-silent bug.
      **Trace:**
      - `convert.py:1007-1034` pre-M212 applied `EOS_FIXES[model_type]` to: top-level config, `text_config`, and `tokenizer_config.json`. Memory A04's claim matched this exactly — the file list was deliberate.
      - `convert.py:1111-1121` (post-fix) byte-copied `generation_config.json` via `_safe_copy`. **Unpatched.**
      - **HF `GenerationMixin` behavior:** `.generate()` reads `model.generation_config.eos_token_id` with PRIORITY over `config.eos_token_id` at call time. If the bundle's `generation_config.json` contains the stale scalar `248044`, the fix in `config.json` is silently overridden.
      - **Live evidence:** `jq '.eos_token_id' /Users/eric/models/Qwen3.6-35B-A3B-JANG_2L/generation_config.json` → `[248046, 248044]`. Multi-EOS list form — both IDs are stop tokens. List-form happens to be safe (both valid stops). **But** the SCALAR form (which some older Qwen3.5 sources ship) would be `248044` alone → silent break.
      - **Verified upstream behavior:** curl'd `https://huggingface.co/Qwen/Qwen3-8B/raw/main/generation_config.json` → `eos_token_id: [151645, 151643]` (list form, different token IDs for newer Qwen3 vocab). The scalar-form risk exists for Qwen3.5-specific source configs that shipped before list-form convention.
      **Fix (iter 143):** extended the eos-fix loop to ALSO patch `generation_config.json` when `eos_fix_map` is non-empty AND the source file exists:
      - Load `source/generation_config.json` as JSON.
      - Handle BOTH forms: scalar `int` (remap via `eos_fix_map[old_eos]`); `list` of IDs (independently map each element via dict.get).
      - Write the patched JSON to the output directory directly.
      - Set `_eos_fixed_gen_cfg = True` so the downstream `extra_configs` byte-copy loop SKIPS this file (otherwise the byte-copy would overwrite the fix with stale source bytes — double-bug).
      - Fall through to normal byte-copy if: no eos_fix_map match for this model_type, or file doesn't exist, or JSON parse fails.
      **Design: load/patch/rewrite, not in-place edit.** Safer because: (a) atomic write via Path.write_text; (b) JSON re-serialization validates structure (catches malformed source); (c) idempotent — re-running convert produces identical bytes.
      **Evidence:** `jang-tools/jang_tools/convert.py:1030-1093` (eos-fix + rewrite). `jang-tools/jang_tools/convert.py:1147-1165` (copy-loop skip guard via `_eos_fixed_gen_cfg`). `python3 -m pytest tests/` full jang-tools suite: 360 passed, 7 skipped — ZERO regressions.
      **Invariants (+4) in new `ralph_runner/tests/test_generation_config_eos_fix.py`:**
      - `test_eos_fix_also_patches_generation_config` — pin the eos-fix region mentions `generation_config.json` + `eos_fix_map`.
      - `test_eos_fix_handles_both_scalar_and_list_forms` — pin `isinstance(old_eos, int)` AND `isinstance(old_eos, list)` branches exist.
      - `test_extra_configs_copy_skips_patched_generation_config` — pin the `_eos_fixed_gen_cfg` guard in the copy loop so the byte-copy doesn't silently overwrite the fix.
      - `test_eos_fix_map_covers_qwen3_5_family` — regression on the `EOS_FIXES` table itself: all 4 Qwen3.5-family model_types (`qwen3_5`, `qwen3_5_moe`, `qwen3_vl`, `qwen3_5_vl`) map 248044 → 248046.
      **Meta-lesson — "file is copied byte-for-byte" ≠ "file is correct".** The M202/M208/M210 lesson generalizes: byte-copy of a config file is correct only if the config's SEMANTIC meaning is the same in the source context and the output context. A source config where `config.json` + `generation_config.json` agree on eos=248044 is self-consistent. After the convert fixes `config.json`'s eos to 248046, byte-copied `generation_config.json` now DISAGREES — the bundle is no longer self-consistent, and HF's runtime picks the wrong value. **Rule: when a convert pass MODIFIES fields in one config, audit every other copy-through config for the SAME field. Byte-identical isn't semantic-identical when the surrounding context changed.** Parallels iter-133 M196's cross-language parity drift — same shape at a different boundary.
      **Meta-lesson — HF's priority order at .generate() is a silent override surface.** `GenerationMixin` prefers `generation_config.eos_token_id` over `config.eos_token_id`. Users debugging "why does my model halt on the wrong token?" don't know which file's value is winning. Publishing a bundle where these disagree is worse than publishing one where both are wrong (at least that's consistent). **Rule: when HF runtime reads the same field from multiple files with priority order, treat the fields as a SET: any convert-time edit must update all of them or NONE.** Applies to `eos_token_id`, `pad_token_id`, `bos_token_id`, `generation_config` defaults like `temperature`/`top_p` if those ever get transformed.
      **Meta-lesson — test byte-AND-semantic for preservation claims.** M202 byte-verified the HF card; iter-143 byte-verified `generation_config.json` preservation AND verified the bundle remains self-consistent after the eos-fix. Future round-3 H audits: for every "copied from source" claim, ask "does the COPY ride the same semantics as the rest of the output, or has the output's semantic shifted?" **Rule: output-correctness includes inter-file consistency. A file that's byte-correct w.r.t. source but inconsistent w.r.t. the bundle is still a bug.**
      **Meta-lesson — load/patch/rewrite > in-place edit for JSON configs.** The fix writes through `json.dumps(gc, indent=2)` rather than line-editing the source bytes. Benefits: JSON re-serialization catches malformed source (bails with a warning rather than shipping garbage); atomic write via Path.write_text is crash-safe; result is idempotent (re-running convert produces identical output). **Rule: for config-transform steps, always go through a JSON round-trip. String-edit-in-place is for text files, not structured configs.**
      **Commit:** (this iteration)
- [x] **M210 (2 Settings lies wired — `outputNamingTemplate` + `defaultOutputParentPath`)** — Iter-142 round-2 angle-I pass (iter-141 was J). Targeted a second surface from M201's candidate-lies list.
      **Trace:**
      - `renderOutputName` grep returned ONLY its own definition + a SettingsWindow preview line + its 2 unit tests. Zero convert-path consumers.
      - `defaultOutputParentPath` grep showed identical pattern: declaration, persist, reset, Snapshot, SettingsWindow UI (TextField + Choose + Clear buttons), but no consumer.
      - **Found the hardcoded site:** `JANGStudio/JANGStudio/Wizard/Steps/ProfileStep.swift:99` `coord.plan.outputURL = src.deletingLastPathComponent().appendingPathComponent("\(src.lastPathComponent)-\(coord.plan.profile)")`. Also at lines 85-89 for the M146 (iter 66) auto-regeneration-on-profile-change path.
      - `src.deletingLastPathComponent()` hardcodes the source's parent — ignoring the user's configured `defaultOutputParentPath`.
      - `"\(src.lastPathComponent)-\(profile)"` hardcodes the format — ignoring the template's pattern tokens.
      - Concrete lie verification: changing Settings → General → Output naming template from `{basename}-{profile}` to `{basename}_{profile}_q` produces ZERO change in the auto-generated folder — the SettingsWindow preview would update, but the actual output dir created by ProfileStep stays on the hardcoded pattern.
      **Fix (iter 142) — PLUMB, don't remove.** Unlike M200's `defaultCalibrationSamples` (which had no downstream use case and was removed), `outputNamingTemplate` + `defaultOutputParentPath` have legitimate power-user value: routing output to a dedicated SSD volume, embedding date/user tokens for organization, using a custom naming convention. So wire them, don't remove.
      **Implementation:**
      - Injected `AppSettings` into `ProfileStep` via `@Environment`.
      - Added `autoOutputURL(for source: URL, profile: String) -> URL` helper that: (a) uses `settings.defaultOutputParentPath` when non-empty AND points at a valid directory (fallback to source's parent when unset or invalid path, avoiding failure cascades); (b) computes the folder name via `settings.renderOutputName(basename: source.lastPathComponent, profile: profile, family: coord.plan.family.rawValue)`.
      - Replaced BOTH hardcoded sites (the `onAppear` initial auto-path + the profile-change regeneration) with calls to this helper. DRY: one helper → both sites drift-proof.
      **Evidence:** `JANGStudio/JANGStudio/Wizard/Steps/ProfileStep.swift:15-18` (AppSettings injection), `:130-160` (autoOutputURL helper), `:85-92` + `:105-107` (helper call sites). `xcodebuild build-for-testing` exits 0. 33/33 AppSettingsTests still pass (including 2 pre-existing `renderOutputName` unit tests that verify template substitution).
      **Invariants (+5) in new `ralph_runner/tests/test_output_path_settings_wired.py`:**
      - `test_profile_step_injects_app_settings` — pin the injection so the settings are reachable.
      - `test_profile_step_calls_render_output_name` — pin `settings.renderOutputName` reference (the template consumer).
      - `test_profile_step_honors_default_output_parent_path` — pin `settings.defaultOutputParentPath` reference.
      - `test_profile_step_no_hardcoded_basename_profile_interpolation` — negative-pin that the pre-M210 shape `\(src.lastPathComponent)-\(` is not in live code (comment-strip first so rationale comments quoting the old pattern don't false-positive).
      - `test_profile_step_has_auto_output_url_helper` — pin the centralizing helper exists (DRY across the two sites).
      **Meta-lesson — round-2 angle-I audits should target the LIE LIST, not re-sweep random fields.** M201's open candidates list gives a prioritized queue of suspected lies. Starting from that list is faster than re-searching the entire Settings surface every iter. **Rule: when a spawned `[ ]` item enumerates candidates, iterate through them before exploring fresh territory. Closes known-gaps faster than greedy breadth-first exploration.** Parallels standard "work off the backlog" discipline but made explicit for the Ralph loop.
      **Meta-lesson — plumb vs remove decision depends on user value, not implementation cost.** M200 removed `defaultCalibrationSamples` because the convert method doesn't need calibration-tunable samples and plumbing it would add complexity for zero user benefit. M210 plumbed `outputNamingTemplate` + `defaultOutputParentPath` because power users DO benefit from configured output organization. **Rule: for each settings lie, ask "does any real user want this setting to take effect?" — if yes, plumb; if no, remove. The right answer isn't always the same.** Inverse of "always remove disconnected fields" — user value overrides implementation simplicity when it's tangible.
      **Meta-lesson — extracting a helper that BOTH sites use is a parity guarantee.** ProfileStep has TWO auto-path sites (onAppear initial + profile-change regeneration). Pre-M210 both hardcoded the same pattern — accidentally consistent. If one site had gotten wired to settings and the other hadn't, the user would see inconsistent behavior: initial auto-path honors the template, but regeneration after profile-change reverts to hardcoded. With `autoOutputURL` helper centralizing the logic, both sites are literally the same code path. **Rule: when two call sites must produce the same output for the same inputs, extract a shared helper. Copy-paste duplication is how drift bugs are born.**
      **Meta-lesson — fall-back to pre-fix behavior when configured value is invalid.** `settings.defaultOutputParentPath` is a raw string the user edited. It might point at a deleted directory, a file (not a dir), or a typo. The helper checks `fileExists + isDirectory` and falls through to `src.deletingLastPathComponent()` on failure. Users who mistakenly clear the setting to a bad path still get a working auto-path. **Rule: when reading user-configured paths as consumed-input, ALWAYS validate them at read time. An invalid configured value should fall through to the default, not propagate an error up the stack.** Parallels iter-129 M192's `JANG_CORS_ORIGINS` default pattern — when the user's config is missing/invalid, use a safe default.
      **Commit:** (this iteration)
- [x] **M208 (Swift ↔ Python tokenizer byte-level parity verified + regression-guarded)** — Iter-141 rotated to **angle J (Bundled-runtime parity)** per tally mandate (J=0 before this iter, needs ≥2 for completion bar §7). Previous iters found architecture + security + UX bugs; this iter proves the RUNTIME CORRECTNESS invariant: same input string → same token IDs across Swift `JANGTokenizer` and Python `AutoTokenizer` on the same bundle.
      **Trace:**
      - `jang-runtime/Sources/JANG/JANGTokenizer.swift:17-349` implements a standalone BPE tokenizer in Swift: byte-level BPE encoder, merges table, special tokens, chat template. Uses `tokenizer.json` + `tokenizer_config.json` from a JANG bundle as its sole input.
      - Python reference path: `transformers.AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained(bundle_dir).encode(text, add_special_tokens=False)` — the upstream canonical tokenizer.
      - **Pre-M208: no test verified the two match.** Existing `JANGTQTokenizerTests.swift` exercised Swift-side wrapper behavior (special-token lookup, chat-template structure) but never ran the same bytes through Python and diffed IDs. A subtle BPE bug in the Swift implementation — wrong merge priority, off-by-one byte-encoder, mishandled space-prefix — would produce plausible-looking output that silently degrades model quality.
      **Live evidence captured iter-141:** ran `python3 -c "from transformers import AutoTokenizer; tok = AutoTokenizer.from_pretrained('/Users/eric/models/Qwen3.6-35B-A3B-JANG_2L'); [print(s, tok.encode(s, add_special_tokens=False)) for s in TEST_STRINGS]"`. Captured reference IDs:
      | Input | Python AutoTokenizer IDs |
      |-------|--------------------------|
      | `"Hello, world!"` | `[9419, 11, 1814, 0]` |
      | `"The quick brown fox jumps over the lazy dog."` | `[760, 3841, 13477, 37550, 33075, 888, 279, 15217, 5388, 13]` |
      | `"What is 2 + 2?"` | `[3710, 369, 220, 17, 478, 220, 17, 30]` |
      Wrote `jang-runtime/Tests/JANGTests/JANGTokenizerPythonParityTests.swift` with these IDs as hardcoded references + `XCTAssertEqual` against Swift `JANGTokenizer(tokenizerPath:).encode(text)` output.
      **Test result: 2/2 parity tests PASS.** Swift output is byte-identical to Python for all 3 strings including the 10-token "quick brown fox" sentence and the numerically-tokenized "2 + 2?" with embedded space-prefix + math operator handling. Concrete command-level evidence:
      ```
      Test Case '-[JANGTests.JANGTokenizerPythonParityTests test_swift_tokenizer_matches_python_reference]' passed (1.019 seconds).
      Test Case '-[JANGTests.JANGTokenizerPythonParityTests test_swift_tokenizer_only_emits_valid_ids]' passed (1.029 seconds).
      ```
      **Test design decisions:**
      - **Fixture skip vs fail:** the 10 MB tokenizer.json isn't in-tree (too large for git). Test uses `XCTSkip` when fixture missing so CI without the model fixture passes via skip (neutral, not red). Developers + Ralph runs with the model pulled exercise full parity. If skip rate rises unacceptably, extract tokenizer.json to a test-only HF repo that CI pulls.
      - **Hardcoded references over live Python call-out:** the Swift test MUST not shell out to Python (forces a Python dep in the Swift test target, slows the test from 2s to 30s+). Captured Python IDs as hardcoded constants + a docstring command for regenerating. Re-capture on any tokenizer.json version bump.
      - **Two tests per fixture:** `test_swift_tokenizer_matches_python_reference` (primary parity) + `test_swift_tokenizer_only_emits_valid_ids` (out-of-vocab regression guard — a bpeEncode bug that emits ID 999999 into the IDs list would bypass the exact-match check if the hardcoded reference happens to also have that ID). Defense in depth.
      - **Test strings chosen deliberately:** ASCII with punctuation (exercises base vocab + comma/period handling), multi-word sentence (merges + space prefixes), and an expression with numbers + mathematical operator (byte-level BPE fallback for non-alphabetic chars). Not chosen: pure emoji or pure CJK (those risk different Unicode normalization behavior across Python/Swift that's legitimate to differ — future extension).
      **Evidence:** `jang-runtime/Tests/JANGTests/JANGTokenizerPythonParityTests.swift` (new, 110 lines). `swift test --filter JANGTokenizerPythonParityTests` exits 0 with 2 passed. Full jang-runtime suite: 64 tests, 4 pre-existing skips, 0 failures.
      **Meta-lesson — parity tests need real reference data, not synthetic fixtures.** `JANGTQTokenizerTests.swift` uses a "tiny vocab" synthetic fixture (line 20: `buildTinyTokenizerDir`). That exercises the LOADER but not the encoder's correctness. Synthetic fixtures verify structural plumbing; real-data references verify SEMANTIC correctness. **Rule: for runtime-parity tests, the fixture MUST be a real model's tokenizer.json + a reference output captured from the canonical implementation. Synthetic fixtures that just exercise code paths give false confidence that encoders produce correct output.** Parallels iter-138 M202's "exercise the NEGATIVE path" — live reference data catches bugs that code-path coverage alone misses.
      **Meta-lesson — angle J must use hardcoded references, not runtime cross-calls.** A test that spawns `python -m tokenize` inside a Swift test is 15x slower + adds a Python dep + is flaky on CI without transformers installed. Capture reference outputs ONCE (document the command), paste as constants, regenerate on fixture version bumps. **Rule: for cross-language parity tests, capture-reference-then-compare is the right pattern. Cross-call-at-test-time makes the test fragile + slow + CI-unfriendly.** Parallels iter-134 M197's substring-in-block approach — pragmatic evidence beats robust but slow infrastructure.
      **Meta-lesson — regression guards formalize existing behavior.** The fact that Swift ALREADY matches Python isn't the point — the test pins that fact against future drift. A small BPE refactor (6 months out) could introduce a subtle bug; without M208, users would see garbage generation before anyone noticed. With M208, the parity test fires the instant the refactor lands. **Rule: when you verify a correctness property manually, codify it. "It works today" ≠ "it'll work tomorrow".** Parallels iter-134 M197's M197 rule: a fix without an invariant has a nondeterministic expiration.
      **Meta-lesson — fixture-skip gives CI/local the right behavior.** XCTSkip reports neutrally (not red) so CI without the 10 MB fixture passes. Local dev with the fixture exercises the real parity. Better than: (a) checking fixture into git (repo bloat), (b) failing when fixture missing (breaks CI), (c) only running in local dev via manual steps (bit-rot). **Rule: for tests requiring a large fixture, use XCTSkip on absence + document the fixture path + acquisition method in the test's doc comment. Best of both worlds: developers with the data exercise the check; CI without it isn't forced red.**
      **Commit:** (this iteration)
- [x] **M206 (SourceStep cold-start guidance — always-visible hint replaces hover-only InfoHint)** — Iter-140 rotated to **angle F (Cold-start stranger)** per angle-tally mandate (F=0 before this iter, needs ≥2 for completion bar §7). Simulated fresh-launch experience: no UserDefaults, no prior source, app open at second 3.
      **Trace:**
      - `JANGStudioApp.swift:11` opens a `WindowGroup("JANG Studio")` → `WizardView()`. Fresh launch lands on `SourceStep` (`WizardCoordinator.active = .source` default).
      - `SourceStep.swift` pre-M206 empty-state content:
        1. Section header "Source model folder" + an `InfoHint` icon.
        2. Row content: `Text("No folder selected").foregroundStyle(.secondary)` (faint, muted) + "Choose Folder…" button.
        3. Explanation of WHAT to pick lived EXCLUSIVELY in the InfoHint tooltip: `"Pick a HuggingFace model directory — one containing config.json and .safetensors shards..."` — hover-only.
      - **Stranger-persona outcome at second 3:** user sees "Source model folder" / "No folder selected" / "Choose Folder…". No instruction. No example. No hint that there's a hoverable (i) icon with help. User is stuck wondering what "model directory" means, what files they need, and whether they can get one somewhere.
      **Fix (iter 140):** added always-visible guidance block INSIDE the folder-picker Section, gated by `coord.plan.sourceURL == nil` so it only shows in the empty state (and disappears when a folder is picked). Three lines of guidance:
      1. `"A HuggingFace model directory contains \`config.json\` and one or more \`.safetensors\` files."` — names the concrete artifacts.
      2. `"Example: ~/Downloads/Qwen3-0.6B-Base/"` — a concrete path a stranger can pattern-match against their Downloads folder.
      3. `Link("Don't have one yet? Browse models on HuggingFace →", destination: https://huggingface.co/models?sort=downloads)` — clickable out to the HF browse page for users with no local model. Sort is `downloads` so the first page shows widely-used models, lowering "which one should I try" friction.
      All three use `.font(.caption)` + `.foregroundStyle(.secondary)` so they're visually subordinate to the main "Choose Folder…" button but clearly legible. `.padding(.top, 4)` separates from the "No folder selected" row.
      **Why NOT a modal/onboarding sheet:** modal onboarding is high-friction and users tend to dismiss without reading. Always-visible inline guidance is more likely to be read AND it naturally disappears once a folder is picked, so returning users aren't pestered.
      **Evidence:** `JANGStudio/JANGStudio/Wizard/Steps/SourceStep.swift:33-75` (new empty-state block). `xcodebuild build-for-testing` exits 0 with only pre-existing warnings.
      **Invariants (+4) in new `ralph_runner/tests/test_source_step_cold_start_guidance.py`:**
      - `test_empty_state_shows_always_visible_guidance` — pin `if coord.plan.sourceURL == nil` gate exists (guidance shows on empty state).
      - `test_guidance_names_required_files` — pin `config.json` AND `.safetensors` are mentioned.
      - `test_guidance_includes_concrete_example_path` — pin a `~/Downloads/` example path exists (regex match).
      - `test_guidance_links_to_huggingface` — pin `huggingface.co` + `Link(` together (clickable, not just text).
      **Meta-lesson — hover-only help is invisible to strangers.** `InfoHint` is a lovely UX affordance for users who know where to look, but a fresh-launch user at second 3 doesn't hover random icons. Cold-start guidance must be always-visible in the empty state. **Rule: for every Step-1-equivalent entry view, if the user-facing text is insufficient to explain the next action WITHOUT mouseover, the view is failing its stranger-proof bar. Move critical hints out of hover-only surfaces.** Parallels iter-135 M198's "pin CAPTURE and RENDER, not just capture" — render must be VISIBLE, not latent.
      **Meta-lesson — concrete examples beat abstract descriptions 10× for cold-start clarity.** `"HuggingFace model directory"` means nothing to a stranger. `~/Downloads/Qwen3-0.6B-Base/` is visually pattern-matchable against whatever they have in their Downloads folder. **Rule: for cold-start guidance, prefer one concrete example path over three sentences of abstract description. Examples are cheap to write, expensive to omit.** Paraphrase of the Unix docs convention: "Show a command invocation, not a man page paragraph, when the reader's goal is to just run the thing."
      **Meta-lesson — escape hatches matter (the HF link).** A stranger who doesn't have a model locally has no obvious next step. Telling them "pick a HuggingFace directory" when they don't have one = dead end. The `Link(... huggingface.co/models?sort=downloads)` provides the escape. `sort=downloads` specifically targets high-quality starter models. **Rule: for any workflow whose first step assumes a precondition the user might not meet, provide a link or button that points them at how to meet that precondition. Don't assume readers arrived with the right setup.**
      **Meta-lesson — angle F validates itself.** Pre-M206 every angle-C (security) iter found real bugs, angle-H caught a fabrication, angle-I caught a setting lie. Angle F targets a DIFFERENT class: UX friction for new users. 10 minutes of "pretend you're a stranger" turned up a gap that 100+ iters of code-focused audits missed because the gap lives in the space of what's ABSENT, not what's broken. **Rule: angle F is essential and should be run with at least a first-launch simulation. The bugs it finds are by-definition invisible to code-scanning alone.**

- [x] **M204 (RunStep disk-space re-check before convert spawn)** — Iter-139 rotated to **angle G (Adversarial user)** per mandate (iter-138 was H). Picked the adversarial scenario "user picks output on a volume, Step 3 preflight passes green, user reads docs for 10 minutes while a concurrent download/Time-Machine snapshot fills the volume, user clicks Continue, Step 4 auto-starts convert, ENOSPC hits at shard 7/15 after 20 minutes of wasted compute".
      **Trace:**
      - `JANGStudio/JANGStudio/Verify/PreflightRunner.swift:170-192` has a sophisticated disk-space gate (M141 iter 63, M173 iter 99, M05 iter 101). Uses `volumeAvailableCapacityForImportantUsageKey` (APFS-aware, accounts for purgeable caches), profile-aware size estimator via `estimateOutputBytes`, and dtype-aware scaling (BF16=2, FP8=1 bytes/weight).
      - `JANGStudio/JANGStudio/Wizard/Steps/ProfileStep.swift:108` calls `PreflightRunner().run(...)` on profile selection. Gate is in Step 3.
      - **The gap:** `JANGStudio/JANGStudio/Wizard/Steps/RunStep.swift:163-167` auto-starts convert via `.onAppear { if coord.plan.run == .idle { runTask = Task { await start() } } }` with ZERO re-verification. Between Step-3 preflight and Step-4 auto-start, arbitrary wall-clock time can pass. Disk state is stale.
      - `start()` pre-M204 went straight from guard → spawn PythonRunner → iterate events. No disk check.
      **Fix (iter 139):**
      - Injected `ProfilesService` into `RunStep` via `@Environment` (matches ProfileStep pattern — no new service, reuses the already-injected one).
      - Added a cheap final disk-space re-check at the top of `start()` BEFORE any state transition or subprocess spawn. Logic:
        1. Read `volumeAvailableCapacityForImportantUsageKey` on the output parent.
        2. Call `PreflightRunner.estimateOutputBytes(plan: coord.plan, profiles: profilesSvc.profiles)` — SAME math as Step 3.
        3. If `estimated > 0 && free < estimated`, set `coord.plan.run = .failed`, append a user-visible log line with both numbers + a next-action, and return.
      - Log message follows `feedback_remediation_pattern.md`: `"Disk space dropped... Need ~X GB, have Y GB free... Free up space or pick a different output folder, then retry."` — symptom + both sides of the gap + action.
      **Evidence:**
      - `JANGStudio/JANGStudio/Wizard/Steps/RunStep.swift:4-10` (ProfilesService injection).
      - `JANGStudio/JANGStudio/Wizard/Steps/RunStep.swift:187-210` (re-check before `run = .running`).
      - `xcodebuild -scheme JANGStudio build-for-testing` exits 0 with only pre-existing warnings.
      - `xcodebuild test-without-building -only-testing:PreflightRunnerTests` passes all 20+ existing tests — the estimator is still correct.
      **Invariants (+5) in new `ralph_runner/tests/test_runstep_disk_recheck.py`:**
      - `test_runstep_imports_profiles_service`: pin the injection so a future refactor can't silently break the re-check.
      - `test_start_fn_calls_estimate_output_bytes`: pin the call to the same estimator Step 3 uses.
      - `test_start_fn_checks_volume_available_capacity`: pin `volumeAvailableCapacityForImportantUsage` — not the plain `Key` variant.
      - `test_start_fn_compares_free_vs_estimated_before_running`: pin the ORDERING — disk comparison MUST happen before `.running` state transition AND before `PythonRunner()` spawn. A future refactor that moves the re-check after the state flip would fail this.
      - `test_start_fn_surfaces_disk_drop_with_actionable_hint`: pin the log message shape — includes "Need ~", "GB free", and an action phrase ("Free up space" / "pick a different").
      **Meta-lesson — time-decay between checks and actions is a real bug class.** Step-3 preflight is a snapshot, not a guarantee. 10 minutes of wall-clock can pass between the check and the action. For cheap checks (< 10 ms), ALWAYS re-run immediately before the action. The cost is negligible; the win is preventing the entire "check was stale" class of failure. **Rule: for every preflight check that gates an expensive action, add a final cheap re-check AT THE ACTION'S CALL SITE, not just in the preflight step. The preflight is for user feedback; the at-site re-check is for actual safety.** Parallels iter-113 M178's "validate at submission AND at fire time" (defense-in-depth for webhook URLs).
      **Meta-lesson — ordering pins are the second-hardest invariant after existence pins.** `test_start_fn_compares_free_vs_estimated_before_running` pins not just "the check exists" but "the check runs BEFORE the state transition AND spawn". Without the ordering pin, a well-meaning refactor could move the check to AFTER `.running` — the check would still fire, but the user would see a brief "starting…" flash before the error, and partial state could leak. **Rule: when a security-adjacent check is composed with state transitions or spawns, pin both existence AND ordering. Invariants should capture the "why" (order matters), not just the "what" (check exists).** Parallels iter-132 M195's startup-backfill ordering pin.
      **Meta-lesson — reuse the EXISTING estimator, don't reimplement.** A naive fix would compute disk space with a fresh formula inside `start()`. That creates a third place-of-truth alongside PreflightRunner + Python `estimate_model.predict`. Three formulas drift. By calling `PreflightRunner.estimateOutputBytes` directly, the Step-3 gate and the Step-4 re-check use literally the same code path — consistency guaranteed. **Rule: when a cross-step check needs math that an earlier step already implemented, CALL the earlier step's function, don't re-derive the math. A single formula-point-of-truth is cheaper to maintain and closes drift bugs before they start.** Parallels iter-134 M197's cross-language parity design.
      **Commit:** (this iteration)
- [x] **M202 (HF model card license lie — fabricated apache-2.0 for any source missing `license` in config.json)** — Iter-138 rotated to **angle H (Output-correctness audit)** per iter-138 mandate (no angle-I repeat). Picked the HF model card as the target artifact — it's the FIRST thing a stranger sees on a public HF listing. Byte-verified the rendered output against a known-licenseless source config and caught a real lie.
      **Trace:**
      - Source: `jang-tools/jang_tools/templates/model-card.md.jinja:2` — `license: {{ license | default("apache-2.0") }}`. Jinja `default` filter fires when `license` is None or missing.
      - `detect_capabilities(model_dir)` in `examples.py:105` reads `"license": cfg.get("license")` — returns `None` if config.json has no `license` key.
      - **Upstream HF reality check (live):** ran `curl https://huggingface.co/Qwen/Qwen3-8B/raw/main/config.json`, parsed JSON, found NO `license` key. HF convention is license-in-README-YAML, not license-in-config.json. Qwen, Llama, Mistral, DeepSeek configs all behave the same way.
      - **Consequence:** every JANG card generated from a vanilla HF source silently claimed `license: apache-2.0` regardless of the source's actual license. Legally concerning for Llama-3 Community, Qwen License, custom NDA-restricted licenses, etc. A fabricated license tag ≠ legal coverage for the publisher.
      **Fix (iter 138):**
      - `modelcard.py`: `generate_card` now returns `(card: str, license_unknown: bool)` so callers see the signal. When config.json lacks `license`, the Python side coerces to `"other"` (HF's standard tag for custom/unknown licenses) and sets `license_unknown=True`.
      - Template: dropped the silent Jinja `default("apache-2.0")` filter. Python now guarantees `license` is always set.
      - Template body: added a visible `> ⚠️ License not detected from source config.json. ... edit frontmatter before HF publishing` warning banner that renders ONLY when `license_unknown=True`.
      - CLI: added a second stderr NOTE (separate from the M91 skeleton warning) specifically naming the license-missing case and pointing at the fix.
      - `--json` output: added `license_unknown` field + coerced fallback from `apache-2.0` to `other`. Swift PublishToHF (future consumer) can gate HF upload on `license_unknown == false` so a careless publisher can't ship a fabricated license.
      - `publish.py`: unpacks the new tuple return, emits a WARNING on stderr BEFORE writing README.md when `license_unknown=True`. User sees the warning regardless of where the generator was invoked from.
      - Jinja comment side-effect: added a `{#- -#}` comment to explain M202, which collapsed the `---` / `license:` newline. Live-rendered evidence showed the frontmatter broken. Removed the decorative comment entirely (lesson: Jinja whitespace-stripping on adjacent raw lines is lethal).
      **Live verification (iter 138):**
      - Built a minimal fixture at `/tmp/m202_demo` with config.json lacking `license` field.
      - Ran `python3 -m jang_tools modelcard --model /tmp/m202_demo` and captured both streams.
      - stdout: card begins `---\nlicense: other\nbase_model: Qwen/Qwen3-0.6B-Base\n...` — verified `license: other`, NOT `apache-2.0`, in the rendered YAML. Body contains the `> ⚠️ License not detected` banner.
      - stderr: BOTH the M91 skeleton warning AND the M202 license warning print. Distinctive phrases; no leakage onto stdout.
      **Tests (+5) in `jang-tools/tests/test_modelcard.py`:**
      - `test_license_present_in_config_round_trips_to_card` — license in config → card has it verbatim, no warning.
      - `test_license_absent_in_config_renders_other_and_warning` — no license → `license: other` + banner.
      - `test_cli_stderr_warns_when_license_absent` — specific stderr phrase when missing.
      - `test_cli_stderr_silent_when_license_present` — no false-positive warning when license is set.
      - `test_cli_json_output_license_unknown_signal` — --json payload carries `license_unknown: true` signal.
      Also updated 4 existing call-sites (`test_card_has_frontmatter`, `test_card_has_usage_section`, `test_modelcard_emits_both_reasoning_and_thinking_tags`, `test_modelcard_omits_thinking_tag_when_not_applicable`) to unpack the new tuple return shape. `test_dry_run_generates_readme` in `test_publish.py` was also broken by the tuple change; fixed via `publish.py` update.
      **Evidence:** `jang-tools/jang_tools/modelcard.py:28-47, 65-91` (Python changes). `jang-tools/jang_tools/templates/model-card.md.jinja:1-2, 34-36` (template changes). `jang-tools/jang_tools/publish.py:114-131` (publish callsite). 360/360 jang-tools tests pass (was 355, +5 new + 4 updated existing). 69/69 jang-server + 17/17 ralph_runner invariants still green.
      **Meta-lesson — silent defaults in templates are fabrications.** Jinja's `default()` filter is a footgun for user-facing output. `{{ license | default("apache-2.0") }}` reads as "use the source's license if set; otherwise fall back". But "fall back to WHAT" is load-bearing: apache-2.0 is a concrete legal claim, not a neutral placeholder. **Rule: for user-facing output that will be PUBLISHED, never use silent defaults on fields with concrete meaning. Either (a) require the value (fail-fast), (b) use a visible placeholder like "unknown" / "other" that the user must replace, or (c) default to the LEAST specific claim (e.g. `"see LICENSE file"`) and make the substitution explicit in the doc.** The apache-2.0 default was picked years ago as "most common"; most-common-ness doesn't make it honest.
      **Meta-lesson — byte-level live verification catches bugs "looks right" testing misses.** The test suite was 100% green before M202 because the test fixtures all set `license` explicitly. No test exercised the PATH where license is None — the default was never triggered by any test. Only live verification (curl real config.json, render real card, read the bytes) surfaced the gap. **Rule: for output-correctness audits, always exercise the NEGATIVE PATH (the fallback, the default, the else-branch). Fixtures that are "representative" usually aren't — they're convenient, and convenient means "set all the fields I remember".** iter-138 validates angle H's "prove byte-for-byte" requirement.
      **Meta-lesson — tuple return shapes break existing callers silently in Python.** Changed `generate_card` from `-> str` to `-> tuple[str, bool]`. Type hint updated but runtime doesn't enforce. Three caller sites continued to work until runtime when their `str` operations on the tuple failed. Python's optional typing means type-shape changes need MANUAL caller audit. **Rule: when changing a return shape, grep for all callers FIRST and update them in the same commit. mypy would have caught this instantly; without mypy, grep is the fallback discipline.** Parallels iter-133 M196's "widen tuple rather than encode via convention" — but explicitly: when you widen, update the CONSUMERS in the same diff.
      **Meta-lesson — Jinja whitespace-strip markers (`-`) are lethal on adjacent raw lines.** My M202 `{#- ... -#}` comment between `---` and `license:` collapsed the two lines into `---license:`. YAML parsers reject that. Only visible via live render. **Rule: Jinja `{#- -#}` whitespace-stripping should never be used inside data-sensitive blocks (YAML, JSON, TOML frontmatter). Use the plain `{# ... #}` form AND visually verify the rendered output whenever you add a comment inside such a block.** Better: skip decorative comments in data blocks entirely.
      **Commit:** (this iteration)
- [x] **M200 (Settings lie removed — `defaultCalibrationSamples` + `calibrationJSONL`)** — Iter-137 rotated to **angle I (Setting-actually-affects-behavior)** after 10 iters of angle-C security work. Picked `defaultCalibrationSamples` (E13 open item: "Calibration sample count setting — verify it actually passes to the Python convert CLI"). Traced end-to-end; confirmed it was a **100% lie** per `feedback_dont_lie_to_user.md`.
      **Evidence chain:**
      - Swift Settings UI: `SettingsWindow.swift:78` shipped a `Stepper(value: $settings.defaultCalibrationSamples, in: 64...1024, step: 64)` in the "Calibration" section of Settings → Advanced.
      - Persistence: `AppSettings.swift:34, 85, 221, 251, 282` — full get/set/Snapshot/load/reset plumbing.
      - Observation: `SettingsWindow.swift:488` registered it in `withObservationTracking`, meaning UI updates triggered on change.
      - **But:** `CLIArgsBuilder.args(for:)` (`JANGStudio/JANGStudio/Runner/CLIArgsBuilder.swift`) emits argv for `jang convert`: `["-m", "jang_tools", "convert", src, "-o", out, "-p", plan.profile, "-m", plan.method.rawValue, "--progress=json", "--quiet-text"]` + optional `--hadamard`. **Zero reference to calibration samples, no conditional emission, no read of `settings.defaultCalibrationSamples`.**
      - Python side: `python3 -m jang_tools convert --help` output (captured inline during iter-137 trace) shows accepted flags = `-o/--output`, `-p/--profile`, `-m/--method`, `--hadamard`. **No `--samples`/`-n` flag on convert.** The `--samples` flag exists only on the separate `profile` subcommand (TurboSmelt routing profile collection, iter-137 trace: `jang-tools/jang_tools/__main__.py:249`).
      - Internal state: `jang-tools/jang_tools/convert.py` grep'd for `n_samples` → zero hits. Convert uses implicit/hardcoded calibration behavior with no external sample-count input.
      - User effect: flipping the Settings Stepper from 64 to 1024 = zero measurable change in convert runtime, output size, or quant quality. Pure UI theater.
      **Bundled cleanup:** `ArchitectureOverrides.calibrationJSONL: URL? = nil` in `ConversionPlan.swift:40` — same pattern. Zero downstream references across the entire JANGStudio codebase. Dead field.
      **Fix (iter 137) — REMOVE, don't plumb.** Rationale for remove-over-plumb: the current convert method (MSE on weights) doesn't need data-dependent calibration. Adding `--samples` to p_convert's argparse + threading through calibrate.py is ~50 lines of Python + test coverage, not trivial. If a future iter adds AWQ/GPTQ/SmoothQuant (which DO use calibration data), reintroduce with the documented protocol (6 steps; see `test_settings_lies_removed.py` module docstring). Reintroduce AFTER end-to-end proof, not before.
      **Removals:**
      - `AppSettings.swift`: deleted `defaultCalibrationSamples` declaration, reset, Snapshot field, Snapshot init, Snapshot apply (5 sites).
      - `SettingsWindow.swift`: deleted the `Section("Calibration") { Stepper(...) }` block and the observation-tracking line.
      - `ConversionPlan.swift`: deleted `calibrationJSONL` field.
      - `AppSettingsTests.swift`: removed the `XCTAssertEqual(s.defaultCalibrationSamples, 256)` assertion.
      - `AppSettingsTests.swift` (bonus): upgraded the backwards-compat `oldSnapshot` decode test with an M200 comment — the blob still contains the removed key, proving `JSONDecoder`'s unknown-key tolerance serves as a migration shim.
      **Invariant (+5) in new `ralph_runner/tests/test_settings_lies_removed.py`:**
      - `test_default_calibration_samples_not_declared_in_live_code`: pin live-code (comment-stripped) absence in `AppSettings.swift`.
      - `test_default_calibration_samples_not_referenced_in_settings_window`: pin live-code absence in `SettingsWindow.swift`.
      - `test_calibration_jsonl_not_declared_in_live_code`: pin live-code absence in `ConversionPlan.swift`.
      - `test_cli_args_builder_doesnt_emit_samples_flag`: defense-in-depth — if someone emits `--samples` argv without also adding argparse support, convert crashes at runtime. Pin.
      - `test_jang_convert_argparse_status_documented`: pin the `__main__.py`'s `p_convert.add_argument` list doesn't include `--samples` or `-n`. If a future iter adds it, the test fires, forcing the reintroducer to also update the Swift side AND this invariant (paired-move constraint).
      **Evidence:** 33/33 AppSettingsTests pass. 5/5 new M200 invariants pass. 69/69 jang-server tests pass. 17/17 collectible ralph_runner invariants pass.
      **Build verification:** `xcodebuild -scheme JANGStudio -quiet build-for-testing` exits 0 with only pre-existing warnings.
      **Meta-lesson — angle rotation surfaces bugs no single angle can see alone.** 10 iters of angle-C security audits wouldn't have found this. Angle C asks "is this code secure?" — a Settings field that does nothing ISN'T insecure, it's just a UX lie. Angle I (Setting-actually-affects-behavior) asks a completely different question and surfaces a whole new class of bug. **Rule: mandatory angle rotation isn't bureaucratic — each angle is a different *lens* that reveals different defects. A checklist that's 100% green on angle C can be riddled with angle-I lies; only full-angle coverage reveals the full state.** iter-137 validates the new F-J angle framework.
      **Meta-lesson — "the field is persisted, therefore it works" is a false inference.** UserDefaults persistence is only the middle layer of the pipeline: UI control → state → persistence → (runtime consumer → behavior change). Testing that the PERSISTENCE round-trips (which AppSettingsTests was doing) proves nothing about whether the value ever reaches behavior. **Rule: for every Settings field, the invariant check isn't "does it persist?" but "does flipping it change observable runtime behavior?" — i.e., proof-of-effect, not proof-of-storage. The lie test must reach the TERMINAL consumer, not stop at the storage layer.** Parallels iter-135 M198's "pin CAPTURE and RENDER, not just capture".
      **Meta-lesson — remove > plumb when the downstream support is missing.** Temptation on discovering a disconnected setting is to "wire it up" — a natural 80-line diff that adds argparse + threading + UI. But that introduces new surface, new tests, new maintenance. If the quant method truly doesn't need the setting (current state: MSE on weights, no data-dependent calibration), REMOVING it is a smaller, safer diff: fewer lines of code, fewer lies, clear reintroduction protocol for the future. **Rule: when a disconnected setting is found, first ask: "is this setting needed at all right now?" Remove by default; plumb only if current behavior genuinely needs user control. A Settings panel with fewer honest knobs is a better UX than one with many lying knobs.**
      **Meta-lesson — document REINTRODUCTION protocols, not just removals.** The `test_settings_lies_removed.py` module docstring has a 6-step protocol for reintroducing the field IF a future quant method legitimately needs it. Without this, the next contributor who thinks "calibration samples would be nice to tune" would re-ship the same lie. With it, the path is clear: plumb Python FIRST, prove end-to-end, THEN add Swift UI. **Rule: for every "removed because dead" item, document the reintroduction protocol in the removal's regression test. Prevents the removal from being seen as a prohibition rather than a placeholder.**
      **Commit:** (this iteration)
- [ ] **M217** — Further runtime-parity sweep beyond tokenization (spawned from M208+M216). Tokenization now has byte-level parity in BOTH directions. Other runtime behaviors where Swift+Python must agree on the same bundle:
      - **Sampler at temperature=0 (greedy):** for identical logits, `argmax` should pick the same token in Swift + Python. Test against a small fixture that dumps logits.
      - **Multi-EOS stop-token handling:** if `eos_token_id = [248046, 248044]`, both runtimes must stop on FIRST match. Any runtime that requires ALL matches would hang.
      - **Chat template apply:** `JANGTokenizer.encodeChatPrompt(system:user:)` vs Python `tokenizer.apply_chat_template(messages, add_generation_prompt=True)`. Non-trivial because templates are Jinja-rendered Python-side, hand-assembled Swift-side.
      - **Codebook dequant result:** JANGTQ's vector quantization — Swift load + dequant vs Python reference must produce bit-identical weight tensors.
      - **SSE framing:** if JANGStudio/jang-runtime consumes SSE from jang-server, frame boundary handling (split on `\n\n`, strip `data: ` prefix, parse JSON) must match.
- [ ] **M215** — Further unicode-path sweep (spawned from M214). Other surfaces that consume filesystem names as identifiers:
      - `outputNamingTemplate` rendering — M210 wired `renderOutputName`; if `{basename}` has emoji/accents, the output folder has them too. That's fine on APFS but HF publish of such output would hit M214. Does the convert → publish flow apply sanitization?
      - Diagnostics bundle filenames (`JANGStudio-diagnostics-<timestamp>.zip`) — timestamp-based, no unicode risk. OK.
      - Log-file paths — `settings.logFileOutputDir` + any filename construction.
      - `JANGTokenizer.swift` → does it handle tokens containing non-ASCII correctly in the BPE encoder's byte-encoder map? (M208 confirmed ASCII inputs match Python; unicode input parity is a round-3 check.)
      - `SourceDetector.swift` passes `url.path` to Python; the subprocess argv path is tested (M214 inspect-source worked). What about the JSON output parsing — does Swift correctly decode `\ud83c\udf55`-escaped strings?

      - `pad_token_id` — does it appear in `config.json`, `generation_config.json`, AND `tokenizer_config.json`? Does convert keep them synced after the fix?
      - `bos_token_id` — same question.
      - `tokenizer_class` — already gets M91-fixed in tokenizer_config; does any other file reference it?

      Apply the M212 "load/patch/rewrite" pattern to any sites with disagreement.

Pre-M210 the preview used the template but the real code path DIDN'T — a textbook "preview lies about the real behavior" bug. Post-M210 they match, but no invariant enforces it.       - **Chat template apply:** does Swift's `JANGTokenizer.encodeChatPrompt(system:user:)` produce identical IDs to Python's `tokenizer.apply_chat_template(messages, add_generation_prompt=True)`? Non-trivial because chat templates are Jinja-rendered Python-side and hand-assembled Swift-side.
      - **Decoding:** `decode(ids)` round-trip must recover the original string for all parity fixtures (already implicit in Python, needs explicit Swift coverage).
      - **Sampler:** temperature=0.0 greedy sampling — same logits → same next-token pick. Check `JANGTQGenerator` vs Python `mlx_lm.generate`.
      - **Stop-token handling:** multiple EOS IDs (MiniMax ships `[200020, 200026]`) — both runtimes must halt on FIRST match, not require both.
      - **SSE framing:** jang-server emits SSE for job streams; if JANGStudio's frontend or jang-runtime parses SSE, frame boundaries must agree.
      - **Codebook dequant result:** JANGTQ codebook vector quantization — Swift load + dequant vs Python reference MUST produce bit-identical weight tensors. Subtle rounding bugs silently degrade quality.
      Each is its own iter. Apply M208's capture-reference-then-compare pattern.
